Writing 10 to the power of 3: 10<sup>3</sup>

Representing water's chemical formula: H<sub>2</sub>O

Denoting ordinal number: 21<sup>st</sup> century ^EZMfesSl

<sup> vs <sub>: <sup> raises text above the baseline; <sub> lowers it.

Presentation vs Semantics: These tags do not carry intrinsic semantic meaning for accessibility or parsing. ^Pm2S7IEl

Using <sup> or <sub> outside of appropriate contexts (e.g., as layout tools rather than for notation)

Nesting <sup> or <sub> inside block-level elements in ways that break inline flow

Forgetting to close tags, resulting in display issues ^42LRlTao

<sup> vs <sub>: <sup> raises text above the baseline; <sub> lowers it.

Presentation vs Semantics: These tags do not carry intrinsic semantic meaning for accessibility or parsing. ^q2sShbG4

In HTML, superscript and subscript are text formatting elements represented by the <sup> and <sub> tags, respectively. The <sup> element displays text slightly above the normal line, typically used for exponents or ordinal indicators (e.g., 1<sup>st</sup>), while the <sub> element positions text slightly below the baseline, often applied in chemical formulas or mathematical notations (e.g., H<sub>2</sub>O). Both elements are inline tags and inherit styling from their parent elements unless explicitly overridden. They are purely presentational and should not be misused for semantic purposes outside of standard notational conventions. ^2dSj9AYD
